2:29:1854:0:14:72:501:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:The Causal Effect of Unemployment Duration on Wages: Evidence from Unemployment
2:30:1933:14:14:72:174:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Insurance Extensions
2:31:1953:14:14:72:366:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Johannes F. Schmieder, Till von Wachter, and Stefan Bender
2:32:2011:14:14:72:234:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:NBER Working Paper No. 19772
2:33:2039:14:14:72:261:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:December 2013, Revised October 2014
2:34:2074:14:28:71:150:630:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:JEL No. J64,J65
2:35:2089:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:36:2097:28:14:71:539:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:This paper provides quasi-experimental estimates of the causal effect of long-term unemployment
2:37:2192:14:14:71:539:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:on wages. Using standard job search theory, the paper derives and tests conditions on reemployment
2:38:2290:14:14:71:539:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:wages under which Unemployment Insurance (UI) extensions can be used as instrumental variables
2:39:2384:14:14:71:539:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:(IV) for unemployment duration. Using a regression discontinuity design, the paper shows that UI
2:40:2480:14:14:71:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:extensions at age thresholds reduced reemployment wages of job searchers in Germany. The UI
2:41:2558:14:14:71:539:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:extensions do not affect the reemployment wages conditional on the month of unemployment exit,
2:42:2652:14:14:71:538:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:implying reservation wages do not bind on average. Hence, UI extensions affect mean wages only
2:43:2746:14:14:71:538:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:through unemployment durations. Our IV estimates imply substantial negative effects of unemployment
2:44:2845:14:42:72:255:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:duration on wages of 0.8% per month.
2:45:2881:42:14:72:183:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Johannes F. Schmieder
2:46:2902:14:14:72:198:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Department of Economics
2:47:2925:14:14:72:160:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Boston University
2:48:2942:14:14:72:168:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:270 Bay State Road
2:49:2960:14:14:72:164:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Boston, MA 02215
2:50:2976:14:14:72:112:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and IZA

2:52:2996:14:28:72:158:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:johannes@bu.edu

2:59:3133:14:14:72:124:210:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and NBER
2:60:3141:14:0:72:196:196:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:tvwachter@econ.ucla.edu
2:61:3164:0:14:306:374:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Stefan Bender
2:62:3177:14:14:306:506:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Institute for Employment Research (IAB)
2:63:3216:14:14:306:414:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Regensburger Str. 104
2:64:3237:14:14:306:394:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:90478 Nuremberg
2:65:3252:14:14:306:351:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Germany
2:66:3259:14:250:306:410:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:stefan.bender@iab.de
2:67:3279:250:14:72:223:100:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:A data appendix is available at:
2:68:3311:14:0:72:283:86:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w19772
3:69:3351:0:33:68:162:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:1  Introduction
3:70:3366:33:21:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:At the peak of the Great Recession, long-term unemployment (unemployment spell lasting
3:71:3452:21:22:68:543:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more than one year) in the United States rose to a historical 5 million individuals, and stands
3:72:3547:22:21:68:543:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at 3.2 million in 2014. In many European countries, long-term unemployment has been a
3:73:3632:21:21:68:543:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:persistent feature of labor markets since at least the early 1980s.  There is an increasing
3:74:3723:21:21:68:543:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:concern among policy makers and academics as to the costs of rising unemployment durations
3:75:3813:21:22:68:543:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to individuals and families, as well as for the labor market and the economy as a whole
3:76:3900:22:21:68:543:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(e.g., Bernanke 2012, Yellen 2014).1However, there are few causal estimates of the effect
3:77:3989:21:21:68:543:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of unemployment duration on wages, earnings, or other outcomes.2This makes it not only
3:78:4075:21:22:68:543:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difficult to assess the costs of long-term unemployment, but also difficult to choose policies
3:79:4169:22:21:68:543:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at both the micro and the macro level.3For example, if nonemployment durations decrease
3:80:4256:21:21:68:543:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reemployment wages, extensions in unemployment insurance (UI) durations – the largest
3:81:4341:21:22:68:543:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government program geared towards job losers in recessions – may hurt the prospects of job
3:82:4431:22:21:68:383:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:losers rather than helping them to obtain better job matches.
3:83:4492:21:21:85:543:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We use the term ‘the causal effect of unemployment durations on job outcomes’ to describe
3:84:4581:21:22:68:543:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:how rising unemployment durations harm the job prospects of unemployed workers..  An
3:85:4665:22:21:68:543:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individual who is unemployed longer may receive different job offers the longer the duration of
3:86:4760:21:21:68:543:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment, e.g. because of skill depreciation or stigma. Thus the worker will effectively
3:87:4852:21:21:68:543:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:face different labor demand solely due to the fact that she has been out of work longer. In
3:88:4943:21:22:68:543:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:addition the worker may accept different jobs the longer she is unemployed (she may have a
3:89:5033:22:21:68:543:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:declining reservation wage), effectively constituting a labor supply response. We define the
3:90:5125:21:18:68:543:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:‘causal effect of unemployment duration’ as the change in reemployment wages that comes only
3:91:5217:18:16:81:543:231:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:1It is widely thought that long unemployment durations can lower reemployment wages and other job
3:92:5314:16:11:68:543:215:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:outcomes of workers via depreciation of skills or because of stigma (e.g., Acemoglu 1995, Machin and Manning
3:93:5422:11:12:68:543:204:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:1999). As a result, long-term unemployment can affect the aggregate labor market and economic recovery
3:94:5524:12:9:68:344:192:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(e.g., Pissarides 1992, Ljungqvist and Sargent 2008, Ball 2009).
3:95:5588:9:15:81:543:183:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:2We found essentially no studies estimating the effect of long-term unemployment on any outcome using
3:96:5689:15:12:68:543:168:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:quasi-experimental variation or within-spell variation from panels. This is reflected in Bernanke (2012) and
3:97:5797:12:12:68:543:156:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Yellen (2014), who do not cite a single empirical study in support of the claim that unemployment duration
3:98:5903:12:12:68:543:144:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:is costly. As discussed below, several studies estimate the depreciation of human capital as one of several
3:99:6010:12:9:68:256:132:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:parameters in models of life-cycle earnings.
3:100:6054:9:15:81:543:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:3Several papers show that the degree of skill depreciation affects the optimal policy mix at the micro level
3:101:6162:15:12:68:543:108:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(e.g., Shimer and Werning 2006, Pavoni and Violante 2007, Pavoni 2009). Moreover, the speed and sources of
3:102:6268:12:12:68:543:96:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:wage loss with unemployment duration have important implications for the potential usefulness of both fiscal
3:103:6376:12:0:68:292:84:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and monetary policy over the short and longer run.
4:104:6427:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from the labor demand side, holding job acceptance decisions (labor supply) constant. This
4:105:6517:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:change in the wage offer distribution throughout the unemployment spell is an important
4:106:6604:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameter as it describes how quickly the job prospects of the unemployed are declining,
4:107:6692:22:21:68:266:647:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:independent from their own decisions.4
4:108:6730:21:21:85:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Existing estimates suggest that the cost of a widespread rise of unemployment duration
4:109:6816:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:could indeed be very large.5However, these estimates potentially overstate the effect of unem-
4:110:6910:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment duration on job outcomes for two reasons. A common concern is that workers with
4:111:6998:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:longer nonemployment durations also have other, potentially unobserved characteristics that
4:112:7089:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:make them hard to employ and lower their wages. Furthermore one would expect that any
4:113:7174:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exogenous manipulation that affects nonemployment durations would also lead to changes in
4:114:7263:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which jobs are accepted by the unemployed. As a result, even estimates free of selection gener-
4:115:7358:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ally recover a combination of effects arising from the individual’s labor supply response (e.g., a
4:116:7456:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:change in reservation wages) and a decline in wage offers in response to longer unemployment
4:117:7548:21:21:68:491:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durations (what we call the causal effect on wages) and are thus hard to interpret.
4:118:7631:21:21:85:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this paper, we provide the first quasi-experimental estimates of the causal effect of
4:119:7719:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment duration on wage offers. These estimates are free of selection and of effects from
4:120:7814:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changes in the reservation wage, and hence reflect true shifts in the wage offer distribution. We
4:121:7911:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:begin by laying out a conceptual framework based on the canonical partial-equilibrium model
4:122:8002:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of job search in which both unemployment duration and reemployment wages are endogenous,
4:123:8090:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which we augment with worker heterogeneity. A classic prediction from the model is that if
4:124:8180:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workers value their outside option, a rise in potential UI durations leads to a decline in job
4:125:8274:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:search intensity and a rise in reservation wages.  A key insight we exploit is that one can
4:126:8365:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:learn about the behavior of reservation wages from observed reemployment wages at different
4:127:8456:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment durations. In particular, we show that if the path of observed reemployment
4:128:8544:21:18:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages does not shift outward in response to a rise in UI durations, this implies that reservation
4:129:8641:18:16:81:543:182:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:4The duration of unemployment is an endogenous variable, determined by individuals’ search effort and
4:130:8742:16:12:68:543:166:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:job acceptance decisions as well as random arrivals of job offers. As in any instrumental variables setting, we
4:131:8853:12:12:68:543:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:identify the effect of unemploment duration that results from explit exogenous variation. Below, we derive
4:132:8959:12:8:68:334:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the mathematical formula for the treatment effect we obtain.
4:133:9019:8:15:81:543:134:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:5Violante and Pavoni (2007) put consensus estimates from structural models (e.g., Keane and Wolpin 1997)
4:134:9123:15:12:68:543:119:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and regression studies (e.g., Addison and Portugal 1989) at 16-23% wage loss per year. For 3.2 million workers
4:135:9233:12:12:68:543:107:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:with unemployment spells longer than one year that implies a loss of over $30 Billion at median earnings.
4:136:9338:12:12:68:543:95:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:This loss is understated since many individuals have unemployment spells longer than one year, and skill
4:137:9442:12:12:68:543:83:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:depreciation is usually specified linearly, implying losses for the many unemployment spells lasting below one
4:138:9552:12:0:68:121:71:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:year as well.
5:139:9566:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages do not bind, at least in the part of the wage offer distribution relevant for workers’
5:140:9658:21:21:68:182:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:employment decisions.
5:141:9679:21:22:85:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:If the condition on reemployment wages are satisfied in the data, the only effect of nonem-
5:142:9770:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment durations on wages must arise from the wage offer distribution changing over the
5:143:9859:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration of unemployment. We derive an expression of the resulting instrumental variables
5:144:9948:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(IV) estimator, show that it obtains a local average treatment effect of unemployment dura-
5:145:10039:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion on wages over individuals whose nonemployment duration responds to the UI extension,
5:146:10128:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and derive an estimable expression of the corresponding weighting function. To gain further
5:147:10219:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:insights on the potential role of reservation wages, which are likely to affect the lower tail of
5:148:10316:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accepted wages, we also extend our approach to estimate the average effect of nonemployment
5:149:10407:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration throughout the wage distribution. Based on the theory, we derive bounds for the
5:150:10495:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:causal effect of nonemployment duration on wages in case the condition on reemployment
5:151:10581:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages does not hold and instead reservation wages do seem to affect job prospects in response
5:152:10674:21:21:68:155:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to UI extensions.
5:153:10691:21:21:85:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We implement our conceptual framework using quasi-experimental variation and data from
5:154:10777:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Germany, which has several features that are ideal for our purposes. During the 1980s, UI
5:155:10866:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durations for middle aged workers in Germany were a step function of exact age at benefit
5:156:10955:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:claiming, such that the causal effect of UI durations on job outcomes can be estimated using
5:157:11047:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a regression discontinuity design. A key feature of the German environment is that we have
5:158:11137:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:access to the universe of social security records with information on day-to-day nonemployment
5:159:11231:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spells, exact dates of birth, as well as a broad range of worker and job characteristics. The
5:160:11324:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:large samples and precisely measured unemployment and earnings information turn out to be
5:161:11413:22:21:68:435:242:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:crucial for estimating the effect of nonemployment durations on wages.6
5:162:11484:21:21:85:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We obtain three main findings. First, we find small but precisely estimated negative effects
5:163:11576:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of UI extensions on wages, job duration, and other job outcomes of middle aged workers, such
5:164:11668:22:17:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the probability of full-time work and working in the same industry and occupation. Second,
5:165:11761:17:16:81:543:161:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:6Similar data is currently not available for the United States, because administrative data do not measure
5:166:11867:16:12:68:543:145:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:exact unemployment and job durations, and samples from survey data are too small. During the period we
5:167:11969:12:12:68:543:133:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:study, the incidence of long unemployment spells and effect of UI extensions on unemployment duration in
5:168:12073:12:12:68:543:121:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Germany were similar to comparable estimates for the United States (Schmieder, von Wachter, and Bender
5:169:12175:12:12:68:543:109:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:2012); the size and structure of wage losses of job losers were similar as in the United States (Schmieder, von
5:170:12286:12:12:68:543:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Wachter, and Bender 2009); it is well known that the structure of earnings in the United States and Germany
5:171:12393:12:0:68:143:85:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:is similar as well.
6:172:12413:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we show that the path of average reemployment wages at different nonemployment durations
6:173:12501:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does not shift, implying that reservation wages do not bind in our setting.  As a result,
6:174:12590:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reservation wages do not contribute to declining wages over the nonemployment spell, and one
6:175:12682:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can use UI extensions as valid manipulation of nonemployment durations. Third, we obtain
6:176:12770:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:IV estimates of the causal effect of nonemployment durations on wage offers. We find that for
6:177:12863:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each additional month in nonemployment duration, average daily wages decline by a bit less
6:178:12953:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than one percent. Thes results are robust to bounds resulting from small effects of reservation
6:179:13048:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages consistent with our wage data. If one extrapolates linearly over the course of six months,
6:180:13144:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this effect can explain about a third of the average wage loss of unemployed workers. This
6:181:13234:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect fades after people have been on a job for a few years and is statistically indistinguishable
6:182:13333:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from zero after five years. This negative effect can arise from multiple sources, including skill
6:183:13430:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depreciation, stigma effects, or changes in job characteristics, something we address explicitly
6:184:13526:22:21:68:197:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in our empirical analysis.
6:185:13552:21:21:85:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our paper is related to several strands of literature. Foremost, it presents both a framework
6:186:13645:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for obtaining causal estimates of the effect of nonemployment durations on wage offers, and a
6:187:13738:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:new set of causal estimates, neither of which is currently available in the literature. Existing
6:188:13834:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates of wage effects are typically based on cross-sectional analyses of nonemployment
6:189:13924:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durations and wages (e.g., Addison and Portugal 1989), or derived from structural models (e.g.,
6:190:14019:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Keane and Wolpin 1997).7While our ordinary-least squares estimates are of similar magnitude
6:191:14110:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as in the existing literature, our IV estimates are about two-thirds to a half of the basic
6:192:14201:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correlation, suggesting a potential role of negative selection in standard estimates. In a recent
6:193:14298:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:paper, using an audit study Kroft, Lange, and Notowidigdo (2013) provided experimental
6:194:14384:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evidence showing that there is a negative causal effect of nonemployment durations on call
6:195:14474:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:back rates for job interviews.  Our paper extends these findings by studying the effect of
6:196:14564:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment on other key outcomes of the employment process, wages and job outcomes,
6:197:14649:22:21:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which are harder to analyze in the context of an audit study because they inherently depend
6:198:14740:21:21:68:249:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the actual employment decision.
6:199:14774:21:21:85:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The parameter we estimate is important for policy. Our findings can be used to assess
6:200:14859:21:18:68:543:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with more confidence the potential cost of rising unenmployment durations for middle aged
6:201:14948:18:16:81:543:97:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:7In an exception, Edin and Gustavsson (2008) document a significant negative effect of nonemployment
6:202:15048:16:12:68:543:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:spells on direct measures of skills in Sweden. Estimates of the earnings losses of displaced workers have also
6:203:15158:12:0:68:463:69:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:been used to infer the correlation of nonemployment duration and wages (e.g., Neal 1995).
7:204:15248:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workers. Since we find that our IV estimate puts weight on all workers exiting unemployment
7:205:15339:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from one to 18 months, our results suggest even shorter increases in unemployment duration
7:206:15429:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may be costly.  Our estimates can be used to calibrate models in macroeconomics or in
7:207:15514:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:public finance in which the causal effect of nonemployment plays an important role. In public
7:208:15607:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance, a growing theoretical literature shows how the structure of labor market depends on
7:209:15699:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the degree of wage decline with nonemployment. For example, Pavoni and Violante (2007)
7:210:15785:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show that this parameter plays a key role when multiple labor market policies are chosen
7:211:15873:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:jointly. In macroeconomics, a series of papers by Ljungqvist and Sargent (2008) argues that
7:212:15964:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:skill depreciation in conjunction with generous UI benefits has led to rising unemployment
7:213:16054:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates in Europe in the 1980s. For the 2008 recession in the U.S., Katz, Kroft, Lange, and
7:214:16143:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Notowidigdo (2013) argue that negative duration dependence may explain part of the lasting
7:215:16233:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rise in long-term unemployment.  In an extension of our main findings, we show that the
7:216:16320:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of unemployment durations on wages appears to be larger in recessionary environments.
7:217:16412:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence, a negative causal effect of nonemployment duration on wage offers may indeed be a
7:218:16500:21:21:68:255:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reason for this duration dependence.
7:219:16536:21:22:85:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our findings also relate to the literature examining the properties and effects of reser-
7:220:16625:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vation wages. Most of the literature is based on survey evidence of reservation wages (e.g.,
7:221:16717:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Feldstein and Poterba 1984, Blau and Robins 1986, DellaVigna and Paserman 2005, Krueger
7:222:16804:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Mueller 2011, 2014). In contrast, here we show that it is possible to infer about the effect
7:223:16900:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of and changes in reservation wages directly when quasi-experimental variation of workers’
7:224:16990:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:outside option is available. As in many other areas of economics, such a revealed-preference
7:225:17082:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approach allows one to side step important measurement issues and hence provides an impor-
7:226:17172:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tant complement to analyses of stated preferences. This is in a similar spirit as Hornstein,
7:227:17264:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Violante, and Krueger (2011), who infer about reservation wages using data on worker flows,
7:228:17355:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and who find, consistent with our results, that in a broad range of search models unemployed
7:229:17447:22:21:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workers’ must place a low value on their outside option.8The best recent evidence on reser-
7:230:17538:21:21:68:543:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vation wages comes from Krueger and Mueller (2014), who find that while reservation wages
7:231:17627:21:18:68:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appear to influence employment decisions among UI recipients in New Jersey, reservation
7:232:17714:18:16:81:543:118:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:8Lalive, Landais, and Zweimueller (2013) replicate our approach of analyzing reemployment wage paths for
7:233:17818:16:12:68:543:102:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Austria and find similar results. In contrast to our findings, and findings by Card, Chetty, and Weber (2007a)
7:234:17928:12:11:68:543:90:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and Lalive, Landais, and Zweimueller (2013) for Austria, Nekoei and Weber (2013) find a larger spike in wages
7:235:18037:11:0:68:447:79:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:at UI exhaustion that induces a slight positive overall effect of UI extensions on wages.
8:236:18127:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages are effectively unaffected by unemployment duration and UI exhaustion.  Hence, as
8:237:18214:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in our setting, changes in reservation wages are unlikely to be responsible for reductions in
8:238:18307:21:22:68:328:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reemployment wages over the unemployment spell.
8:239:18354:22:21:85:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our paper also adds to the literature estimating the effect of UI benefits on nonemploy-
8:240:18442:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment durations and job outcomes. While a substantial body of research has documented the
8:241:18530:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disincentive effect of UI benefits (for example, Moffitt 1985; Katz and Meyer 1990; Meyer 1990;
8:242:18625:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rothstein 2011, Kroft and Notowidigdo 2012, Schmieder, von Wachter, and Bender 2012a,b,
8:243:18712:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Farber and Valletta 2013), a much smaller literature has found mixed results regarding the
8:244:18802:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects on wages and other job outcomes based on research designs using observational stud-
8:245:18893:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ies (e.g., Addison and Blackburn 2000). More recent studies by Lalive (2007), Card, Chetty
8:246:18983:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Weber (2007a), and Centeno and Novo (2009) used regression discontinuity designs to
8:247:19070:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more clearly identify the effects and find negative impacts on wages. While these results are
8:248:19163:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively imprecisely estimated and hence not statistically significantly different from zero,
8:249:19258:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:confidence intervals contain possible negative and positive values that are economically mean-
8:250:19352:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ingful.9In addition to providing more precise estimates, partly due to larger sample sizes, the
8:251:19447:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:framework in this paper also allows an empirical assessment of the sources behind the wage
8:252:19537:22:39:68:189:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects of UI extensions.
8:253:19562:39:33:68:130:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2  Theory
8:254:19571:33:22:68:543:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We use a discrete time, non-stationary search model (e.g. van den Berg 1990) to derive our
8:255:19661:22:21:68:543:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:main findings in three steps. First, we show how the effect of UI extensions on reemployment
8:256:19753:21:21:68:543:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages can be decomposed into changes in reservation wages and changes in the wage offer
8:257:19840:21:21:68:543:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution over the nonemployment spell.10Second, we use the model to show how the
8:258:19924:21:22:68:543:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of UI extensions on the reemployment wagepath(i.e., reemployment wages conditional
8:259:20013:22:21:68:543:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the time of exiting unemployment) can be used to infer about the response of reservation
8:260:20104:21:18:68:543:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages to UI extensions. Third, we show that if the reemployment wage path is unaffected, it is
8:261:20198:18:15:81:543:152:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:9Consistent with a negative effect of nonemployment durations, Black, Smith, Berger and Noel (2003) find
8:262:20302:15:12:68:543:137:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:positive effects on reemployment and quarterly earnings of UI recipients who are randomly assigned to (but
8:263:20408:12:12:68:543:125:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:not necessarily participate in) more intensive job search services. Meyer (1995) reports imprecisely estimated
8:264:20518:12:12:68:543:113:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:positive effects on earnings for UI recipients who receive a bonus upon faster reemployment. Degen and Lalive
8:265:20627:12:12:68:543:101:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(2013) find negative earnings effects from a reduction in potential UI benefit durations in Switzerland in a
8:266:20735:12:9:68:199:89:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:difference in difference design.
8:267:20767:9:0:77:446:80:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:10For an early insightful discussion of these issues, see Addison and Portugal (1989).
9:268:20854:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:possible to identify the average change in the wage offer distribution over the nonemployment
9:269:20947:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spell – and hence the causal effect of nonemployment durations on wages – using UI extensions
9:270:21040:21:39:68:245:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as a source of exogenous variation.
9:271:21075:39:29:68:189:630:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.1  Setup of Model
9:272:21094:29:21:68:543:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Workers become unemployed in periodt=  0, are risk neutral and maximize the present
9:273:21177:21:21:68:543:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discounted value of income. In each period workers receive UI benefitsbtand choose search
9:274:21266:21:21:68:543:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intensityλt, which is normalized to be equal to the probability of receiving a job offer in that
9:275:21362:21:22:68:543:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period. Without loss of generality we focus on the case of a two-tiered UI system, where UI
9:276:21453:22:21:68:544:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:benefits are at a constant levelbup to the maximum potential duration of receiving UI benefits
9:277:21547:21:21:68:543:495:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:P. After benefit exhaustion, individuals receive a second tier of payments indefinitely, so that
9:278:21643:21:22:68:543:474:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:bt=bfor allt≤Pandbt=bfor allt > P. The cost of job searchψ(λt)is an increasing,
9:279:21722:22:21:68:275:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:convex and twice differentiable function.
9:280:21763:21:21:85:543:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Jobs offer a wagew∗tand wage offers are drawn from a distribution with cumulative distri-
9:281:21852:21:22:68:543:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bution functionF(w∗;μt), which may vary with the duration of unemploymentt, for example
9:282:21939:22:21:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:due to skill depreciation or stigma. To simplify the exposition we assume that the distribution

14:590:33279:39:29:68:285:630:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.5  Heterogeneity and Nonlinearity
14:591:33314:29:21:68:543:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The results generalize to the case of heterogeneous workers and nonlinear changes in reem-
14:592:33404:21:21:68:543:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment wage path. Allowing for heterogeneity in our context is important since it makes
14:593:33493:21:21:68:543:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it clear that our estimates of the effect of UI extensions on the path of reemployment wages
14:594:33585:21:22:68:543:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may be affected by dynamic selection. As we further discuss in Section 3.3, selection may
14:595:33674:22:21:68:543:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entail either higher or lower ability individuals searching longer or responding more strongly
14:596:33768:21:21:68:543:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to UI incentives. In the theory, heterogeneity is purposefully kept completely flexible. In our
14:597:33863:21:22:68:543:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:empirical analysis, we resolve the problem of dynamic selection using our quasi-experimental
14:598:33955:22:21:68:148:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:research design.
14:599:33971:21:21:85:543:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Heterogeneity is also important because in its presence our IV estimates will be a weighted
14:600:34062:21:22:68:543:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average of the individual-specific treatment effects. Moreover, since skill depreciation is not
14:601:34157:22:21:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessarily linear throughout the nonemployment spell, the IV estimates will also be an average
14:602:34252:21:21:68:543:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over different parts of the potentially nonlinear skill depreciation schedule.  To be able to
14:603:34345:21:22:68:543:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interpret the IV estimate, we derive an expression for the IV estimator and its weighting
14:604:34434:22:21:68:113:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function.

16:707:37759:30:21:85:543:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Proposition 1 states that the IV estimator from a regression of wages on nonemployment
16:708:37845:21:21:68:543:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durations using UI extensions as an instrument has an interpretation of a local average treat-
16:709:37939:21:21:68:543:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment effect of unemployment durations on wages. The weighting functionω∗(t)is proportional
16:710:38029:21:22:68:543:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the differences in survivor functions. The IV estimator puts more weight on those individ-
16:711:38122:22:21:68:543:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:uals whose nonemployment durations respond more strongly to the instrument (i.e., whose
16:712:38209:21:21:68:543:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:survival functions are shifting).  This is akin to the standard result in linear models with
16:713:38301:21:22:68:543:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneous parameters (Angrist, Imbens, and Rubin 1996), but is here derived for the gen-
16:714:38393:22:21:68:543:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eral case in which wages may be a nonlinear function of nonemployment durations (Angrist,
16:715:38482:21:21:68:543:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Graddy, and Imbens 2000). Hence, as in the more standard linear case, the weighting function
16:716:38574:21:22:68:543:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be estimated from the data. In the empirical section, we discuss the weighting function,
16:717:38666:22:21:68:543:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discuss how the IV estimator is affected if the underlying conditions of Propositions 1 fail, and
16:718:38763:21:38:68:537:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we present bounds for the case in which there are small shifts in the reservation wage path.
16:719:38855:38:29:68:264:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.6  Empirical Content of Model
16:720:38886:29:21:68:543:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The main results do not depend on the particular model of wage setting. The contribution
16:721:38974:21:21:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the theory is to show that estimating whether the path of reemployment wages is affected
16:722:39065:21:22:68:543:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by changes in the UI benefit path (or other factors affecting the value of nonemployment),
16:723:39155:22:21:68:543:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provides a test for the importance of the outside option of unemployed workers in the wage
16:724:39245:21:21:68:543:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determination process. If reemployment wages conditional on unemployment duration do not
16:725:39333:21:22:68:543:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:respond to changes in the outside option, then the decline of reemployment wages over the
16:726:39422:22:21:68:543:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment spell can not be due to a response to the the outside option throughout the
16:727:39510:21:21:68:543:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment spell. Instead, it must be due to a decline of the wage offer distribution over the
16:728:39606:21:21:68:543:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment spell. For this to be meaningful, individuals must value the outside option,
16:729:39696:21:22:68:543:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as implied by a change in hazard rates. The theory suggests a straightforward strategy for
16:730:39786:22:21:68:543:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the empirical work. Another key insight is that using weak additional assumptions implied by
16:731:39878:21:0:68:543:68:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the theory, one can estimate the effect of UI extensions on the path of reemployment wages
17:732:39970:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:even if the distribution of characteristics throughout the nonemployment spell changes. We
17:733:40060:21:21:68:502:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will return to our empirical approach after briefly describing the institutional set up.
17:734:40148:21:22:85:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:While we illustrated this insight in a model of wage posting, a symmetric intuition applies
17:735:40239:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in wage bargaining models, where wages should in principle also be affected by the outside
17:736:40329:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:option of the unemployed worker. If they are not, then changes in the value of the outside
17:737:40419:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:option throughout the unemployment spell should also not have an effect on reemployment
17:738:40506:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages and thus cannot explain the observed decline in reemployment wages. A similar intuition
17:739:40599:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would hold in a directed search model where workers choose to search for jobs in a segment of
17:740:40692:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the labor market. In such a model wages are affected by the choice of the labor market and
17:741:40782:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the reservation wage when searching in a market. If the wage conditional on unemployment
17:742:40870:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration does not respond to UI benefit changes, then the choice of which segment to search
17:743:40961:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in is not responding to changes in the outside option and the outside option cannot explain
17:744:41052:22:39:68:325:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the decline in wages over the unemployment spell.
17:745:41101:39:33:68:336:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3  Institutions, Data and Empirical Methods
17:746:41144:33:29:68:246:383:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.1  Institutional Background
17:747:41173:29:21:68:543:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:After working for at least 12 months in the previous three years, workers losing a job through
17:748:41267:21:22:68:543:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no fault of their own in Germany are eligible for UI benefits that provide a fixed replacement
17:749:41361:22:21:68:543:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate of 63 percent for an individual without children.16This paper focuses on the time period
17:750:41454:21:21:68:543:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between 1987 and 1999, which is the longest period for which the UI system was stable, and
17:751:41544:21:22:68:543:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:during which the maximum duration of benefits was tied to the exact age of the start of benefit
17:752:41639:22:21:68:543:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:receipt and to prior labor force history. Between July 1987 and March 1999, the maximum
17:753:41726:21:21:68:543:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential UI duration for workers who were younger than 42 years old was 12 months.17For
17:754:41814:21:21:68:543:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workers age 42 to 43 maximum potential UI duration increased to 18 months and for workers
17:755:41903:21:22:68:543:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age 44 to 48, the maximum duration further rose to 22 months. Workers with lower prior
17:756:41989:22:21:68:543:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:labor force attachment also experienced increases in potential UI durations at the 42 and
17:757:42078:21:18:68:543:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:44 age cutoffs, albeit smaller.  Our main identification strategy is to use the variation in
17:758:42170:18:16:77:543:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:16For individuals with children the replacement rate is 68 percent. There is a cap on earnings insured, but
17:759:42277:16:11:68:543:107:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:it affects only a small number of recipients. Since they are derived based on net earnings, in Germany UI
17:760:42382:11:9:68:482:96:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:benefits are not taxed themselves, but can push total income into a higher income tax bracket.
17:761:42476:9:15:77:543:87:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:17For a description of other cutoffs present in the system and recent reforms, see Schmieder, von Wachter,
17:762:42582:15:0:68:157:72:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and Bender (2012a).
18:763:42603:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential UI durations at the age thresholds to analyze unemployment, wages, and the effect
18:764:42694:21:38:68:271:690:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of nonemployment duration on wages.18
18:765:42731:38:29:68:127:652:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.2  Data
18:766:42740:29:21:68:543:623:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For this paper we have obtained access to the universe of social security records in Germany
18:767:42832:21:22:68:543:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from 1975 to 2008. The data covers day-to-day information on every instance of employment
18:768:42921:22:21:68:543:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covered by social security and every receipt of unemployment insurance benefits, as well as cor-
18:769:43017:21:21:68:543:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding wages and benefit levels. We observe several demographic characteristics, namely
18:770:43108:21:22:68:543:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gender, education, birth date, nationality, place of residence and work, as well as detailed job
18:771:43204:22:21:68:543:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics, such as average daily wage, occupation, industry, and characteristics of the
18:772:43297:21:21:68:125:495:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:employer.19
18:773:43308:21:22:85:544:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For our analysis sample, we extracted all unemployment insurance spells where the claimant
18:774:43398:22:21:68:543:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:was between age 40 and age 46 on the claim date. We consider unemployment spells starting
18:775:43487:21:21:68:543:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:any time between July 1987 and April 1999. For each UI spell we created variables about
18:776:43574:21:21:68:543:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the previous work history (such as job tenure, labor market experience, wage, industry and
18:777:43664:21:22:68:543:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:occupation at the previous job), the duration of UI benefit receipt in days, the UI benefit
18:778:43755:22:21:68:425:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:level, and information about the next job held after non-employment.
18:779:43823:21:21:85:543:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since we do not directly observe whether individuals are unemployed we follow the previous
18:780:43913:21:22:68:543:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:literature and, in addition to duration of UI benefit receipt, we use length of non-employment
18:781:44007:22:21:68:543:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as a measure for unemployment durations (e.g., Card, Chetty, and Weber 2007b). The du-
18:782:44093:21:21:68:543:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ration of non-employment is measured as the time between the start of receiving UI benefits
18:783:44184:21:22:68:543:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the date of the next registered period of employment. Our analysis period assures that
18:784:44274:22:21:68:452:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we can follow individuals for at least 9 years after the start of the UI spell.
18:785:44353:21:21:85:543:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We calculate each individual’s potential UI duration at the beginning of the UI spell,
18:786:44439:21:18:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using information about the law together with information on exact birth dates and work
18:787:44526:18:15:77:543:179:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:18In Germany individuals who exhaust regular UI benefits are eligible for means tested unemployment
18:788:44625:15:12:68:543:164:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:assistance benefits (UA), which do not have a limited duration. The nominal replacement rate is 53%, but
18:789:44729:12:12:68:543:152:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:UA payments are reduced substantially by spousal earnings and other sources of income, which may explain
18:790:44833:12:12:68:543:140:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:why only about 50% of UI exhaustees take up UA benefits. In Schmieder, von Wachter and Bender (2012a)
18:791:44934:12:9:68:299:128:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:we provide an in-depth assessment of the role of UA.
18:792:44986:9:15:77:543:119:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:19Individual workers can be followed using a unique person identifier. Since about 80 percent of all jobs are
18:793:45095:15:12:68:543:104:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:within the social security system (the main exceptions are self-employed, students, and government employees)
18:794:45204:12:12:68:543:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:this situation results in nearly complete work histories for most individuals. Each employment record also
18:795:45310:12:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:has a unique establishment identifier that can be used to merge establishment characteristics to individual
18:796:45417:12:0:68:124:68:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:observations.
19:797:45432:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:histories. This method yields exact measures for workers who have been employed for a long
19:798:45522:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:continuous time and hence are eligible for the maximum potential benefit durations for their
19:799:45614:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age groups. However, the calculation is not as clear cut for workers with intermittent periods
19:800:45708:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of unemployment because of complex carry-forward provisions in the law.  We thus define
19:801:45795:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our core analysis sample to be all unemployment spells of workers who have been employed
19:802:45883:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for at least 36 months (44 months at the age 44 cutoff) of the last seven years and who did
19:803:45974:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not receive unemployment insurance benefits during that time period.20In Schmieder et.
19:804:46060:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:al. (2012a), we show that the characteristics of this sample are comparable with those of UI
19:805:46152:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recipients of similar age in the United States. In addition, in our sensitivity analysis we also
19:806:46248:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consider results when we use all workers affected by the two age cutoffs, irrespective of prior
19:807:46343:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:labor force history. While for these we cannot obtain the marginal effect of an additional
19:808:46433:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:month of UI extension, we show that we can obtain consistent IV estimates of the effect of
19:809:46523:22:38:68:455:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment duration under the same conditions as in our main sample.
19:810:46594:38:29:68:163:417:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3  Estimation
19:811:46609:29:21:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The institutional structure and data allow us to estimate the causal effect of UI durations on
19:812:46703:21:21:68:543:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages. In addition, it allows us to verify the conditions on the path of reemployment wages
19:813:46794:21:22:68:543:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:described in Section 2 even in the presence of dynamic selection. As a result, it can be used
19:814:46887:22:21:68:543:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to obtain estimates of the causal effect of nonemployment duration on wages. Our empirical
19:815:46977:21:38:68:272:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strategy follows three consecutive steps.
19:816:47018:38:21:68:543:265:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Estimating the Causal Effect of UI Durations on Employment and Wages.The
19:817:47090:21:21:68:543:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:institutional structure and data allow us to estimate the causal effect of large extensions in UI
19:818:47187:21:22:68:543:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:benefit durations on non-employment duration, reemployment wages and other outcomes for
19:819:47274:22:21:68:543:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workers with previously stable employment using a regression discontinuity design. We follow
19:820:47366:21:21:68:543:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:common practice and first show smoothed figures to visually examine discontinuities at the
19:821:47456:21:22:68:543:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eligibility thresholds (e.g., Lee and Lemieux 2010). To obtain estimates for the main causal
19:822:47548:22:18:68:543:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects, we follow standard regression discontinuity methodology and estimate variants of the
19:823:47641:18:15:77:543:119:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:20Individuals who have quit their jobs voluntarily are subject to a 12 weeks waiting period. To focus on
19:824:47745:15:12:68:543:104:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:individuals who lost their job involuntarily and minimize selection concerns due to quitting we restrict our
19:825:47853:12:0:68:438:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:sample to individuals who claimed UI benefits within 12 weeks after their job ended.
20:826:47939:0:39:68:206:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following regression model:
20:827:47966:39:39:204:543:672:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:yi=β+γ×∆P×Dai≥a∗+f(ai) +-i,(8)
20:828:47996:39:21:68:543:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereyiis an outcome variable, such as non-employment duration (D) or reemployment wages
20:829:48084:21:21:68:544:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(w), of an individualiof ageai.Dai≥a∗is a dummy variable that indicates that an individual
20:830:48174:21:16:68:543:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is above the age thresholda∗. In the notation from Section 2, we obtain estimates fordDdPand
20:831:48266:16:10:69:91:575:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f16:F:dE[w]
20:832:48271:10:17:75:95:565:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:dP.
20:833:48274:17:21:85:543:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For our main estimates, we focus on the period from July 1987 - March 1999, and we use
20:834:48360:21:22:68:543:527:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sharp threshold at age 42. We estimate equation (8) locally around the two cutoffs and
20:835:48450:22:21:68:544:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specifyf(ai)as a linear function while allowing different slopes on both sides of the cutoff.
20:836:48543:21:21:68:543:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We use a relatively small bandwidth of two years on each side of the cutoff, and summarize
20:837:48633:21:22:68:543:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our extensive sensitivity analysis below.In order to obtain additional power we also estimate a
20:838:48728:22:21:68:543:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pooled regression model, where we take the estimation samples for the age 42 and the age 44
20:839:48819:21:21:68:543:420:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cutoffs together.21For this procedure we normalize the age for all individuals within two years
20:840:48914:21:21:68:543:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the age 42 (44) threshold to the age relative to age 42 (44) (i.e. the rescaled age variable
20:841:49009:21:22:68:543:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is set to 0 for someone who is exactly age 42 (44) at the time of claiming UI). We estimate
20:842:49100:22:21:68:543:356:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:the following model on the pooled sample:yi=β+γ×∆P×Dai≥a∗+f(ai) +-i,whereai
20:843:49175:21:21:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the normalized age variable and∆Pis the average change in potential UI durations at the
20:844:49265:21:22:68:543:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age threshold. With this specificationˆγis a direct estimate of the rescaled marginal effect,
20:845:49358:22:21:68:543:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forcing it to be equal at the two cutoffs. We always present regression discontinuity robust
20:846:49450:21:38:68:360:271:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:standard errors based on Calonico et al. (forthcoming).22
20:847:49507:38:21:68:543:233:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Estimating the Shift in the Path of Reemployment Wages and Hazards.The main
20:848:49582:21:21:68:543:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:goal of the paper is to estimate the causal effect of nonemployment durations on wages. As
20:849:49672:21:21:68:543:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:derived in Section 2, the first step in obtaining such an estimate is to assess whether the path
20:850:49768:21:22:68:543:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of reemployment wages and the reemployment hazard shift in response to the UI extensions.
20:851:49857:22:17:68:543:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:While estimating the shift is in principle straightforward, a key issue is the potential presence
20:852:49954:17:15:77:543:131:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:21We also estimated all results at the age 44 cutoff separately. The point estimates are very similar but lack
20:853:50064:15:9:68:109:116:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:precision.
20:854:50074:9:15:77:543:107:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:22Optimal bandwidth computations (as in Imbens and Kalyanaraman, 2012, and Calonico et al., forth-
20:855:50172:15:12:68:543:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:coming) are computationally quite demanding due to the large number of observations, especially when we
20:856:50275:12:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:calculate dynamic effects. We therefore keep the bandwidth at 2 years, but report optimal bandwidth estimates
20:857:50384:12:0:68:265:68:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:for the main results in our robustness checks.
21:858:50432:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of dynamic selection. For example, low skilled workers may be more credit constrained, and
21:859:50522:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hence respond more strongly to UI extensions. Even absent changes in UI benefits, it is likely
21:860:50616:21:22:68:414:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that less productive workers have longer nonemployment durations.
21:861:50681:22:21:85:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the absence of selection, we could directly estimate the average shift in the reemployment
21:862:50774:21:0:68:374:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:B:wage path and test whether it is equal to zero. Letδ=E
21:863:50828:0:7:376:397:637:10:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f15:F:[∂we
21:864:50832:7:8:393:416:630:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f16:F:i(t,P)
21:865:50838:8:0:393:403:622:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f10:F:∂P
21:866:50840:0:11:417:422:637:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:F:]
21:867:50841:11:21:426:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:be the average shift in
21:868:50864:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the reemployment wage path. To obtain an estimate ofδ, one would estimate the following
21:869:50951:22:40:68:416:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regression on the sample above and below the respective age cutoffs
21:870:51018:40:0:231:289:543:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f9:C:w∗i=δPi+
21:871:51026:0:25:296:306:556:8:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f13:F:T∑
21:872:51028:25:0:292:306:531:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f16:F:t=1
21:873:51031:0:39:308:543:543:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:θt+f(ai) +-i(9)
21:874:51046:39:21:68:543:504:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wherew∗iis the observed reemployment wage,θtare time dummies for the duration of non-
21:875:51131:21:22:68:543:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:employment, andf(ai)is a polynomial in age.  Yet, althoughcov(P,-)  =  0from the RD
21:876:51214:22:21:68:543:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions, the resulting estimate forδfrom this regression is inconsistent because nonem-

21:879:51479:22:21:68:543:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the estimated OLS coefficientˆδis anupper boundfor the trueδ.Our analysis of observable
21:880:51566:21:21:68:543:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics of individuals exiting at different durations and our contrast of the IV and OLS
21:881:51662:21:21:68:543:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimators of the effect of nonemployment on wages in Section 5 support the assumption that
21:882:51753:21:22:68:413:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less able individuals tend to have longer nonemployment durations.
21:883:51819:22:21:85:543:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This is sufficient for our purposes, because from the theory we know that the reservation
21:884:51908:21:0:68:336:291:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:wage has to rise or stay constant and hence that∂w
