21:891:52181:17:21:68:543:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we find that the estimatedˆδis close to zero, given thatˆδis an upper bound of the trueδ, we
21:892:52273:21:22:68:543:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can conclude that the entire reemployment wage path and hence reservation wages have not
21:893:52361:22:21:68:543:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shifted. Below, we will also use the confidence interval for the estimateˆδto derive bounds for
21:894:52456:21:21:68:361:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our causal estimates for small shifts in reservation wages.
21:895:52515:21:22:85:543:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We will also graphically examine the reemployment wage path, as well as a rich set of
21:896:52600:22:21:68:543:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predetermined characteristics of workers exiting at different points in the nonemployment
21:897:52689:21:21:68:543:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spell. If the distribution of observed characteristics over the duration of nonemployment is
21:898:52781:21:0:68:543:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unaffected by UI extensions, then this provides further direct evidence for the absence of a
22:899:52875:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strong role of selection. Similar arguments based on observables can be made as for estimates
22:900:52968:21:38:68:223:690:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of the reemployment hazard.23
22:901:52997:38:22:68:543:652:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Estimating the Causal Effect of Nonemployment Durations on Wages.If the haz-
22:902:53073:22:0:68:468:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:B:ard rate declines (dhtdP<0) and there is no change in reemployment wages (E
22:903:53148:0:8:470:491:642:10:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f15:F:[∂we
22:904:53152:8:8:487:509:634:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f16:F:i(t,P)
22:905:53158:8:0:487:497:626:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f10:F:∂P
22:906:53160:0:12:511:516:642:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:F:]
22:907:53161:12:21:520:544:630:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:A:= 0)
22:908:53165:21:21:68:543:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then the relevant conditions for Proposition 1 hold, and the effect of UI durations on reem-
22:909:53257:21:21:68:543:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment wages are driven solely by higher nonemployment durations. The final step then is
22:910:53347:21:22:68:543:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to directly estimate the causal effect of nonemployment duration on wage offers using poten-
22:911:53439:22:21:68:543:545:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tial UI durations as instrumental variables for nonemployment durations. By the results in
22:912:53529:21:21:68:543:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Section 2.3, the resulting IV estimator obtains the average effect of nonemployment duration
22:913:53621:21:22:68:543:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on wages for all individuals responding to the UI extension, irrespective of elapsed nonem-
22:914:53712:22:21:68:543:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment duration. Below, we will calculate the weighting function of the IV estimator over
22:915:53803:21:21:68:543:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the nonemployment spell. As explained in Section 3.2, we also extend our IV strategy and
22:916:53891:21:22:68:543:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:use the age cutoff itself as instrument for nonemployment duration for the broader sample of
22:917:53983:22:38:68:385:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workers for whom we cannot calculate potential UI durations.
22:918:54043:38:29:68:229:379:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.4  Validity of RD Design
22:919:54069:29:21:68:543:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A key aspect in all three steps of our empirical strategy is the validity of the RD design.
22:920:54160:21:21:68:543:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The regression discontinuity method only yields consistent results if factors apart from the
22:921:54252:21:22:68:543:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:treatment variable do not vary discontinuously at the threshold.  In our setting, both UI
22:922:54341:22:21:68:543:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:claimants and their employers face potential incentives to manipulate the age of claiming. We
22:923:54434:21:21:68:543:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have examined this issue at length in our related paper (Schmieder, von Wachter, and Bender
22:924:54525:21:21:68:543:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2012a) and its Web Appendix, and conclude that sorting around the threshold is not a concern
22:925:54617:21:22:68:543:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in this case. We only summarize the main findings here and refer the interested reader to our
22:926:54710:22:21:68:543:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:precursor paper for a more detailed discussion of manipulation, including potential reasons
22:927:54801:21:21:68:145:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for its absence.
22:928:54817:21:22:85:543:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A standard test for sorting around the threshold is to investigate whether the density of
22:929:54906:22:21:68:543:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observations shifts or spikes near the threshold (McCrary 2008). Figure 1 (a) shows the number
22:930:55000:21:18:68:543:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of unemployment spells in two-week age intervals around the cutoff. There is a small shift in
22:931:55093:18:15:77:543:98:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:23Most of the literature presents estimates of the effect of UI durations on reemployment hazards without
22:932:55198:15:0:68:250:83:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:specifically addressing this selection issue.
23:933:55245:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observations from two weeks before to two weeks after the age cutoffs, that affects only about
23:934:55339:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:200 individuals relative to about 500,000 observations in the sample close to the age cutoff.
23:935:55432:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Further investigation showed that this increase is not driven by individuals who postpone their
23:936:55527:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:claim, but that, if at all, the incidence of separations rises slightly at the eligibility age. To
23:937:55625:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investigate the nature of sorting further we investigated whether predetermined characteristics
23:938:55720:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vary discontinuously at the threshold. Figure 1 (b) shows the pre-unemployment log wage in
23:939:55810:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2 month bins around the thresholds and shows no discernible discontinuity. We investigated
23:940:55900:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:many other baseline characteristics and found that only the fraction of UI recipients who
23:941:55989:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are female is estimated to increase statistically significantly by about 0.8 percentage points.
23:942:56084:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:All other variables show essentially no (economically or statistically) meaningful difference
23:943:56177:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at the threshold.24In smaller datasets, such minor discontinuities and density shifts would
23:944:56268:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:almost certainly not be detectable. While these findings point to a small violation of the RD
23:945:56361:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identification assumptions, these should have a relatively small impact on the overall results.
23:946:56456:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In fact, neither trimming observations close to the eligibility thresholds nor directly controlling
23:947:56555:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for observable characteristics affects our results. To ensure that our results are not affected by
23:948:56653:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sorting around the threshold and by particular implementation choices of the RD estimator,
23:949:56743:22:39:68:533:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we performed multiple robustness checks summarized in the sensitivity section (Section 6).
23:950:56833:39:33:68:393:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4  The Average Effect of UI extensions on Job Quality
23:951:56886:33:29:68:448:298:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.1  The Effects of UI extensions on Nonemployment Durations
23:952:56946:29:22:68:543:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We begin by replicating our findings on the effect of UI extensions on UI duration and nonem-
23:953:57039:22:21:68:543:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment duration from our previous paper (Schmieder, von Wachter, and Bender 2012a),
23:954:57124:21:21:68:543:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which we will later use to calculate IV estimates of the effect of nonemployment duration on
23:955:57216:21:21:68:543:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages. Increases in potential UI durations have a very clear effect on nonemployment dura-
23:956:57306:21:22:68:543:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions and hence substantially change behavior of unemployed individuals. Showing averages
23:957:57395:22:21:68:543:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by two-months age windows, Figure 2 (a) shows that increasing potential UI durations at
23:958:57482:21:21:68:543:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the two age thresholds leads to substantial increases in UI durations. This effect is partly
23:959:57574:21:18:68:543:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanical, since individuals who would have exhausted their benefits at 12 months or 18
23:960:57662:18:16:77:543:102:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:24There is a tiny difference in the years of education variable at the first threshold of about 0.03 years (or
23:961:57772:16:0:68:164:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:10 days) of education.
24:962:57796:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:months are now covered for up to 6 more months, and partly behavioral, since individuals
24:963:57884:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may reduce their search effort and thus stay unemployed longer. The purely behavioral effect
24:964:57976:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of an increase in potential UI durations is demonstrated in Figure 2 (b), which shows the
24:965:58065:22:21:68:251:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect on nonemployment durations.
24:966:58099:21:21:85:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In Table 1, columns (1) and (2) confirm the visual impression. The effects on actual UI
24:967:58186:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration and nonemployment duration are very precisely estimated. The table also shows the
24:968:58276:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal effect of an increase in potential UI durations by 1 month, i.e. the estimated RD
24:969:58366:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:coefficient rescaled by the increase in potential UI durations. For one additional month of
24:970:58457:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential UI benefits unemployed individuals receive about 0.3 months of additional benefits
24:971:58549:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and remain unemployed for about 0.15 months longer.  These marginal effects are similar
24:972:58636:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to findings from previous research including Moffitt (1985), Katz and Meyer (1990), Meyer
24:973:58725:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1990) Card, Chetty, and Weber. (2007a), or Lalive (2007), although much more precisely
24:974:58812:22:21:68:121:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimated.
24:975:58822:21:21:85:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, as further discussed in von Wachter, Bender, and Schmieder (2012b), column (3)
24:976:58909:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of 1 shows that the probability of ever again working in a social security liable job decreases
24:977:59004:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by about 0.5 (0.1) percentage points per additional month of potential UI benefits at the age
24:978:59097:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:42 threshold (pooled). In the sensitivity section, we will assess whether this small effect could
24:979:59194:21:38:68:442:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imply a potential bias from sample selection in our main wage estimates.
24:980:59266:38:29:68:416:311:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.2  The Effect of UI Extensions on Reemployment Wages
24:981:59320:29:21:68:543:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As discussed in the theory section, longer nonemployment durations in response to higher po-
24:982:59412:21:22:68:543:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tential UI durations could either raise wages as individuals have more time to search for a bet-
24:983:59508:22:21:68:543:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ter job, or lower wages if the negative effect from longer nonemployment durations dominates.
24:984:59601:21:21:68:543:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 3 (a) shows the effect on the log wage at the first job after the period of unemployment.
24:985:59697:21:22:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:There appears to be a small decline by about 0.01 log points in the post-unemployment wage
24:986:59787:22:21:68:543:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at the age 42 threshold.  At the age 44 threshold, the lines (fitted quadratic polynomials)
24:987:59878:21:21:68:543:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also seem to indicate a small drop in the post-unemployment wage. Figure 3 (b) shows the
24:988:59966:21:22:68:543:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference in the pre-unemployment log wage and the post-unemployment log wage.  This
24:989:60051:22:21:68:543:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference is a way to remove an individual fixed effect and hence can be viewed as a way to
24:990:60143:21:21:68:543:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both control for possible selection into employment and to obtain more precise estimates by
24:991:60234:21:0:68:543:69:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:controlling for predetermined characteristics. The figure shows that the average wage loss for
25:992:60330:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the unemployed in our sample is substantial, ranging from 13% to 16%. While the gain in
25:993:60417:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:precision is modest, Figure 3 (b) indicates that selection along the previous wage has little
25:994:60510:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:impact on the results, and again clearly points to a negative effect of a rise in potential UI
25:995:60604:22:21:68:274:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durations on post-unemployment wages.
25:996:60641:21:21:85:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The corresponding regression estimates in Table 1 columns (4) and (5) show that increases
25:997:60730:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in potential UI durations lead to precisely estimated negative effects on post-unemployment
25:998:60821:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages. Panel A shows that the post-unemployment wage is about 0.8 percent lower in both
25:999:60908:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:levels and first differences when potential UI durations increase by six months.  Panel B
25:1000:60997:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shows the results from pooling both cutoffs and reveals similar estimates with a small gain in
25:1001:61091:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:statistical precision. The estimate from the pooled model implies that an increase in potential
25:1002:61186:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UI durations by one month decreases post-unemployment wages by about 0.1 percent. Below
25:1003:61273:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we show that these small effects of UI extensions on wages can imply substantial negative
25:1004:61362:22:21:68:303:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects of nonemployment durations on wages.
25:1005:61406:21:21:85:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although the effect on the initial wage obtained after reemployment shown in Table 1 is
25:1006:61493:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small, the losses can add up to more substantial effects if individuals remain in lower paying
25:1007:61587:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:jobs for a long period of time. Table 2 shows the effect on the log wage one, three, and five
25:1008:61680:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:years after the start of the new employment spell. The estimates decline from one to five
25:1009:61769:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:years start of employment, consistent with the result in Table 2 that there is a small positive
25:1010:61864:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(yet insignificant) effect of potential UI durations on wage growth. Yet, although the longer-
25:1011:61958:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:term effects are not estimated precisely, the point estimates after 5 years are suggestive of
25:1012:62051:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potentially substantial cumulated wage losses. We will return to the implications for the total
25:1013:62146:21:22:68:334:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wage loss and individual behavior in the conclusion.
25:1014:62198:22:21:85:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Other papers that have estimated the wage effect of increases in potential UI durations
25:1015:62285:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have found similar point estimates, although generally with less precision than we do. For
25:1016:62375:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:example Card, Chetty and Weber (2007a) found a negative point estimate of UI durations
25:1017:62461:22:21:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on wages, quite comparable when rescaled to a marginal effect.  Similarly, van Ours and
25:1018:62548:21:21:68:543:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Vodopivec (2008) and Centeno and Novo (2009) find negative effects of similar magnitude of
25:1019:62638:21:21:68:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UI extensions. As further discussed in Section 5, an additional value added with respect to
25:1020:62729:21:22:68:543:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these papers is that we provide a framework and dynamic results that allow us to separate
25:1021:62818:22:0:68:305:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the wage offer and the reservation wage effect.
26:1022:62867:0:29:68:409:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.3  The Effect of UI Extensions on Other Job Outcomes
26:1023:62921:29:21:68:543:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In this section we show that individuals do not simply accept lower wages in return for other
26:1024:63014:21:21:68:543:658:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:desirable job characteristics – i.e., jobs tend to be worse among all the dimensions we can
26:1025:63105:21:22:68:543:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measure here.  Columns (1) to (4) of Panel B of Table 2 show the effect of increases in
26:1026:63192:22:21:68:543:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential UI durations on a number of job-related outcome variables. The first outcome is the
26:1027:63285:21:21:68:543:594:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:completed job tenure at the post-unemployment job, which is often used as an indicator of the
26:1028:63378:21:22:68:543:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quality of the job match. Column (1) of Panel B shows that there is a small decrease in the
26:1029:63469:22:21:68:543:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration of the post-unemployment job of about 0.0081 years in Panel A, which is a decline
26:1030:63559:21:21:68:543:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of about 1% relative to mean post-unemployment job tenure (it is statistically significant at
26:1031:63652:21:22:68:543:509:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a 10% level for the full sample, see the Web Appendix). This confirms findings in Table 1
26:1032:63741:22:21:68:543:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that higher potential UI durations reduce job stability even beyond the initial spell. Hence, it
26:1033:63837:21:21:68:543:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does not appear individuals with longer UI durations trade lower wages for more stable jobs
26:1034:63928:21:22:68:315:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or jobs that appear to represent better matches.
26:1035:63976:22:21:85:543:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We analyzed several additional indicators of job quality. Longer potential UI durations
26:1036:64063:21:21:68:543:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decrease the probability of finding a full time job, but although precisely estimated the effect
26:1037:64159:21:21:68:543:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is less than 1% relative to the mean of 89% (column (2) of Panel B).25An important finding of
26:1038:64252:21:22:68:543:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the literature on displaced workers is that those switching to another industry or occupation
26:1039:64345:22:21:68:543:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:experience much larger declines in earnings (e.g., Neal 1995, Addison and Portugal 1989).
26:1040:64434:21:21:68:543:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence, one would expect that longer UI durations may help individuals to find jobs in their
26:1041:64525:21:22:68:543:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:previous line of work. Columns (3) and (4) of Panel B of Table 2 show that this is not the case.
26:1042:64621:22:21:68:543:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Longer potential UI durations increase the probability of switching to a different industry and
26:1043:64716:21:21:68:456:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a different occupation by about 0.12 to 0.18 percentage points, respectively.
26:1044:64793:21:22:85:543:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, all measures of job quality available in our data either point to negative effects
26:1045:64884:22:21:68:543:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of longer potential UI durations or no effect. Hence, at least based on this limited set of job
26:1046:64979:21:21:68:543:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics, it does not appear that workers with longer UI durations accept lower wages
26:1047:65071:21:22:68:543:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in return to better job outcomes along other dimensions. The analysis of other job outcomes
26:1048:65162:22:21:68:543:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also provides insights into the potential channels underlying the reduction in wages and the
26:1049:65254:21:18:68:406:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:role of nonemployment durations, which we further discuss below.
26:1050:65318:18:15:77:543:107:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:25We also analyzed changes in firm size as proxy for employer quality, as well as the probability of a rise in
26:1051:65428:15:0:68:263:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:commuting, and found no significant change.
27:1052:65473:0:33:68:525:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5  The Causal Effect of Nonemployment Durations on Reemployment Wages
27:1053:65542:33:29:68:383:675:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1  Selection Throughout the Nonemployment Spell
27:1054:65591:29:21:68:543:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A key step in estimating the causal effect of nonemployment duration on wages is to assess
27:1055:65681:21:22:68:543:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the response in hazard rates and reemployment wages throughout the nonemployment spell.
27:1056:65768:22:21:68:543:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Although we will directly control for selection below, to assess the potential for dynamic
27:1057:65858:21:21:68:543:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection we begin with a descriptive analysis of the evolution of observable characteristics
27:1058:65951:21:22:68:543:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:throughout the nonemployment spell.  As summary measures Figure 4 shows the mean of
27:1059:66034:22:21:68:543:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pre-unemployment wages (a) and the mean of predicted reemployment wages (b) (based on a
27:1060:66121:21:21:68:543:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:broad range of pre-determined characteristics) by month of nonemployment duration. Vertical
27:1061:66212:21:21:68:544:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bars indicate that the point estimates at timetare statistically significant at the 5 percent
27:1062:66305:21:22:68:543:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:level.  As expected, there is some correlation between pre-determined characteristics and
27:1063:66394:22:21:68:543:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment duration, though the gradient is not very strong. For example, mean pre-
27:1064:66480:21:21:68:543:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unemployment wages fall by about 5% and mean predicted wages fall by about 7% in the
27:1065:66564:21:22:68:543:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first year of nonemployment duration. In separate analysis, we found that years of schooling
27:1066:66656:22:21:68:543:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or fraction female is positively correlated with nonemployment duration. More importantly
27:1067:66745:21:21:68:543:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for our analysis, in both of these figures the pre-unemployment wage paths and the predicted
27:1068:66837:21:22:68:543:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reemployment wage path are essentially unaffected by changes in potential UI durations.
27:1069:66924:22:21:68:543:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:While there are a few statistically significant point estimates in each figure (and in the figures
27:1070:67022:21:21:68:543:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of single characteristics not shown here), given that each figure is created from 24 separate
27:1071:67115:21:22:68:543:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:point estimates, it is expected that about one to two of the estimates are statistically significant
27:1072:67215:22:21:68:543:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the 5 percent level purely because of sampling variation.26Overall, these figures therefore
27:1073:67309:21:21:68:543:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:support the notion that the distribution of observable characteristics over the nonemployment
27:1074:67402:21:21:68:543:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spell is essentially uncorrelated with potential UI durations, suggesting that it is unlikely that
27:1075:67500:21:18:68:543:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential UI durations exert a strong effect on the distribution of unobservable characteristics.
27:1076:67597:18:16:77:543:181:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:26The one exception appears to be the spikes at the exhaustion point for fraction female. Individuals who
27:1077:67702:16:12:68:543:165:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:are exiting from unemployment at the exhaustion points are significantly more likely to be female. This is
27:1078:67808:12:12:68:543:153:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:consistent with larger labor supply effects of UI benefits for women. The fact that the spikes in fraction women
27:1079:67920:12:12:68:543:141:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:cancel each other out, seems to indicate that some women are simply waiting until their benefits expire before
27:1080:68030:12:12:68:543:129:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:going back to work. To address this aspect, we show in the sensitivity section that our results hold within
27:1081:68137:12:0:68:132:117:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:gender groups.
28:1082:68153:0:29:68:455:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Estimates of the Shift of Reemployment Hazards and Wages
28:1083:68214:29:21:68:543:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 5 shows estimates of the shift in the hazard rate at the age 42 discontinuity. We clearly
28:1084:68310:21:21:68:543:658:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:see that the hazard rate shifts downward in response to increasingPfor all nonemployment
28:1085:68398:21:22:68:543:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durationstsmaller than the maximum potential UI durationP. This is statistically significant
28:1086:68490:22:21:68:543:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for nearly all point estimates, even in the first period (t= 0), so individuals are clearly forward
28:1087:68589:21:21:68:543:594:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:looking and responding to the increase inPa long time before they are running out of benefits.
28:1088:68683:21:22:68:543:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A similar pattern has been observed in many other studies of the effect of UI extensions on
28:1089:68774:22:21:68:401:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment duration (e.g., Card, Chetty, and Weber 2007b).
28:1090:68835:21:21:85:543:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 6 Panel (a) shows the effect of changes inPon the reemployment wage conditional
28:1091:68921:21:22:68:543:509:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ont. On average, wages decline by about 25 percent within the first year. However, we do not
28:1092:69013:22:21:68:543:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observe a corresponding change in the path of reemployment wages over the nonemployment
28:1093:69100:21:0:68:473:466:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:spell.  In the notation of the model of Section 2, it appears that indeed∂w
28:1094:69175:0:13:473:495:475:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f16:F:ei(t,P)
28:1095:69182:13:17:473:543:462:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:∂P=  0for
28:1096:69191:17:22:68:543:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all nonemployment durationst < P. In the Web Appendix we show an almost unchanged
28:1097:69272:22:21:68:543:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pattern when we control for individual heterogeneity by plotting the difference in post and
28:1098:69363:21:21:68:543:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pre unemployment log wage. Extending UI benefits does not shift the reemployment wage
28:1099:69448:21:21:68:141:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:path upwards.
28:1100:69461:21:22:85:543:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The only statistically significant changes in the reemployment wages are at the exhaustion
28:1101:69551:22:21:68:543:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points for the two groups, when reemployment wages go down relative to the other group. It is
28:1102:69644:21:21:68:543:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:noteworthy that the two downward spikes are of very similar magnitude and essentially cancel
28:1103:69736:21:22:68:543:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each other out. These differences are reduced when we look at women and men separately,
28:1104:69823:22:21:68:543:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indicating that the negative wage spikes are partly driven by more women exhausting UI
28:1105:69909:21:21:68:111:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:benefits.
28:1106:69918:21:22:85:543:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The evidence in Section 5.1 and theoretical considerations discussed in Section 3.3 suggest
28:1107:70009:22:21:68:543:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it is unlikely that these findings are overturned by a change in the distribution of worker
28:1108:70100:21:21:68:543:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics over the nonemplyoment spell. As outlined in Section 3.3, relying on our RD
28:1109:70191:21:22:68:543:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions, we can obtain direct estimates of the mean shift in the reemployment wage
28:1110:70277:22:21:68:543:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:paths that are not affected by dynamic selection. Table 3 presents estimates of theaverage
28:1111:70367:21:0:68:273:125:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f8:C:shiftin the reemployment wage path,E
28:1112:70403:0:8:275:296:137:10:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f15:F:[∂we
28:1113:70407:8:8:292:315:129:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f16:F:i(t,P)
28:1114:70413:8:0:292:302:121:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f10:F:∂P
28:1115:70415:0:12:316:321:137:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f13:F:]
28:1116:70416:12:21:321:543:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:, obtained from implementing equation (9).
28:1117:70458:21:21:68:543:104:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Column (1) of Table 3 shows the results controlling for a linear effect of nonemployment
28:1118:70546:21:0:68:544:83:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration. This yields an estimate forδfor the 12 to 18 month discontinuity very close to
29:1119:70636:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zero (point estimate -0.016% with a standard error of 0.048%). If we control more flexibly
29:1120:70726:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the nonemployment duration effect (Columns 2 to 3), the point estimate is even closer to
29:1121:70818:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:0. Given that the estimates in Table 3 are very close to zero, and that theory excludes cases
29:1122:70911:22:0:68:115:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for which
29:1123:70920:0:11:120:154:654:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f16:F:∂wei(t,P)
29:1124:70929:11:0:132:447:643:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:∂P<0, this confirms the visual impression of Figure 6 that
29:1125:70987:0:11:452:486:654:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f16:F:∂wei(t,P)
29:1126:70996:11:17:463:543:643:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:∂P= 0for all
29:1127:71008:17:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment durationst < P. This shows that the value of the outside option, in this case
29:1128:71099:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the potential UI duration, does not affect reservation wages and therefore that the effect of
29:1129:71192:22:21:68:534:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UI durations on wages found in Section 4 arises due to a rise in nonemployment durations.
29:1130:71281:21:21:85:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:These results imply that reservation wages do not appear to bind in our sample. This
29:1131:71365:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is consistent with related findings in the literature. For example, DellaVigna and Paserman
29:1132:71456:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2005) calibrate a model similar to ours and find that very few wage offers fall below the
29:1133:71546:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reservation wage. Our results are also consistent with structural estimates in van den Berg
29:1134:71637:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1990) who found that most job offers are indeed accepted and that unemployed workers do
29:1135:71725:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not seem to reject many jobs based on wages. Similarly, Hornstein, Krusell, and Violante
29:1136:71813:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2011) show that in broad classes of search models, the value of non market time – and hence
29:1137:71905:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the reservation wage – has to be low to be able to reconcile why despite high wage dispersion,
29:1138:71999:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and hence a high option value of searching, workers in practice accept jobs quickly. Following
29:1139:72093:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our approach, Lalive, Landais, and Zweimueller (2013) also find that the path of reemployment
29:1140:72186:21:21:68:394:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages does not respond to increases in UI durations in Austria.
29:1141:72249:21:22:85:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In contrast, Krueger and Mueller (2014) find that jobs with wages above the self-reported
29:1142:72338:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reservation wage are more likely to be accepted, although a substantial fraction of jobs paying
29:1143:72433:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:below the reservation wage are accepted as well.  However, they also find that reservation
29:1144:72523:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages do not change significantly throughout the nonemployment spell within individuals,
29:1145:72611:22:0:68:482:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nor do they respond to UI exhaustion. Hence, in our notation these results imply
29:1146:72691:0:11:487:520:249:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f16:F:∂wei(t,P)
29:1147:72700:11:17:495:543:238:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f9:C:∂φit>0
29:1148:72706:17:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but∂φit∂P=∂φit∂t= 0. In this case the first two terms in equation (5) are still equal to zero
29:1149:72799:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the IV estimator discussed next recovers the causal effect of unemployment duration on
29:1150:72889:22:38:68:101:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages.
29:1151:72895:38:29:68:517:140:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.3  Estimates of the Causal Effect of Nonemployment Durations on Wages
29:1152:72966:29:21:68:543:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The results on the hazard and reemployment wage path imply that reservation wages do not
29:1153:73054:21:21:68:543:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bind. As a result, the observed decline in reemployment wages is entirely due to the decline
29:1154:73146:21:0:68:543:69:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the wage offer distribution (equation 1), and the effect of UI durations on wages is only due
30:1155:73244:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to a rise in nonemployment durations (equation 5). Proposition 1 then allows us to obtain
30:1156:73333:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a valid estimate of the average decline in the reemployment wage path. In the final step of
30:1157:73424:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our empirical analysis, we thus estimate the slope of the reemployment wage path using UI
30:1158:73513:22:0:68:430:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:B:durations as instrumental variables for nonemployment durations:π=
30:1159:73579:0:7:436:455:658:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f28:F:dE[w]
30:1160:73584:7:12:441:451:651:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:F:dPdD
30:1161:73588:12:0:441:450:639:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:F:dP
30:1162:73590:0:21:458:461:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:.
30:1163:73591:21:21:85:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 4 shows 2SLS results for the effect of nonemployment durations on reemployment
30:1164:73675:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages using extensions in potential UI durations as an instrument. The table first shows the
30:1165:73767:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first stage regression (i.e., the effect of UI extension on nonemployment durations), which
30:1166:73858:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:easily passes weak instrument concerns. The second column shows the ’reduced form’ of the
30:1167:73947:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:IV estimator, which correspond to the baseline estimates of the effect of potential UI durations
30:1168:74043:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on wages of Section 4.2. Column (3) reports the resulting 2SLS estimate of nonemployment
30:1169:74131:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:durations on wages. We find thatπ=−0.78%, which is precisely estimated. Thus, our main
30:1170:74217:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finding is that an additional month of nonemployment lowers average wage offers of middle
30:1171:74306:22:21:68:248:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aged workers by about 0.8 percent.
30:1172:74340:21:21:85:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To better understand the nature of our IV estimator, recall that Proposition 1 states that in
30:1173:74433:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the presence of heterogeneity and nonlinearity in the slope of the reemployment wage function,
30:1174:74527:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the IV estimator obtains the local average treatment effect of wage declines for individuals
30:1175:74619:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whose nonemployment durations are most affected by the instrument. As such, it is weighted
30:1176:74709:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:towards the treatment effects of compliers to the UI extensions that underlie our regression
30:1177:74801:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discontinuity (RD) estimates.  As seen from the survival functions in Panel (b) of Figure
30:1178:74890:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:5 the compliers come from the entire range of nonemployment durations, with the largest
30:1179:74977:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weight being between 12 and 18 months. Hence, the IV estimator estimates an average of the
30:1180:75067:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of nonemployment duration on wages over a broad spell of nonemployment durations.
30:1181:75155:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In contrast to the IV estimator, the implicit weighting function of the OLS estimator puts
30:1182:75245:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more weight on long durations where there are fewer individuals but for whom the gradient is
30:1183:75337:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:flatter. As a result the, OLS estimator for the full sample (column 3 of Table 4) is similar to
30:1184:75432:22:21:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the IV estimate. To obtain a better comparison, we reestimated the OLS estimator excluding
30:1185:75522:21:21:68:543:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individuals with spells longer than 18 months that would typically receive little weight in
30:1186:75613:21:21:68:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:surveys with much smaller sample sizes. The resulting estimate corresponds more closely to
30:1187:75703:21:22:68:441:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what is shown in Figure 6, and is approximately double the IV estimate.
30:1188:75774:22:21:85:543:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To gauge the magnitude of our estimates, our point estimates imply a loss in daily wages
30:1189:75862:21:0:68:543:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of 4.8% (9.6%) for 6 (12) additional months of nonemployment duration. Based on Figure 6,
31:1190:75953:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this represents about 40% of the average wage loss at 6 and 12 months, respectively. Thus,
31:1191:76043:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the causal effect of nonemployment spells explain a substantial fraction of the average wage
31:1192:76135:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:loss at job loss. Since the causal effect we estimate here is likely due to multiple channels
31:1193:76228:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:– including skill depreciation, discouragement, or stigma – it is not clear what magnitude
31:1194:76318:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to expect. While it is hard to compare our estimate with previous findings based on non-
31:1195:76406:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:experimental estimates, the findings fall in the same broad range. Estimates based on the
31:1196:76495:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correlation of nonemployment duration of displaced workers with reemployment wages suggest
31:1197:76585:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects bigger than our IV estimate, and similar to our censored OLS estimate (e.g., Addison
31:1198:76677:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Portugal 1989), but as explained above may be affected by selection.27Estimates of the
31:1199:76767:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate of depreciation of human capital during unemployment based on structural models show
31:1200:76856:21:38:68:497:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:results of similar order of magnitude as our findings (e.g., Keane and Wolpin 1997).
31:1201:76940:38:29:68:363:460:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.4  Analysis of Wage Distribution and Bounding
31:1202:76987:29:21:68:543:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The finding in Table 3 and Figure 6 (a) provide strong evidence that UI extensions do not affect
31:1203:77083:21:22:68:543:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reemployment wages through changes in reservation wages. Even with large extensions that
31:1204:77171:22:21:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:clearly affect the hazard rate and a large administrative dataset the implied effect of changes
31:1205:77266:21:21:68:543:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the reservation wage on the mean reemployment wage is a precisely estimated zero. To
31:1206:77353:21:22:68:543:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investigate whether our focus on the mean (even though this is the correct measure in our
31:1207:77442:22:21:68:543:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model) masks small effects of the reservation wage at the bottom of the wage distribution
31:1208:77531:21:21:68:543:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(where one might expect the largest effect), we used our large sample sizes to analyze the full
31:1209:77626:21:21:68:543:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of wages. The percentiles of the wage distribution by nonemployment duration
31:1210:77715:21:22:68:543:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for those above and below the 12 month cut off point are shown in Figure 6 (b) (as before
31:1211:77804:22:21:68:543:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those RD estimates that are significant are shown with vertical bars). The figure clearly shows
31:1212:77899:21:21:68:543:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the evolution of the wage distribution with nonemployment duration as it shifts downwards
31:1213:77988:21:22:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and fans out. If a response in reservation wages to UI extensions mattered, one should see the
31:1214:78082:22:21:68:543:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect mostly at the bottom of the wage distribution. Figure 6 (b) indeed shows that there
31:1215:78172:21:21:68:543:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appears to be a significant rise in the lower quantiles of the wage distribution in response to
31:1216:78267:21:22:68:543:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UI extensions. However, the rise at the first cutoff and appears to be offset by a decline at the
31:1217:78364:22:18:68:543:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:second cutoff. As in case of mean wages in Figure 6 (a), this crossing of the reemployment
31:1218:78454:18:16:77:543:93:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:27Absent quasi-experimental evidence or detailed worker characteristics, Addison and Portugal (1989) ad-
31:1219:78558:16:0:68:281:77:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:dress selection using a Heckman correction term.
32:1220:78608:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wage path can only be explained by dynamic selection and suggests the pattern may be due to
32:1221:78699:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a selective shifting from one exhaustion point to the next. To directly assess this possibility,
32:1222:78795:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we applied the same procedure as with the mean in Section 5.2 to the cumulative density
32:1223:78882:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function (CDF) of reemployment wages for the entire sample. Columns 3 to 5 of Table 3
32:1224:78967:21:21:68:542:626:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:show estimates of the mean shift of selected points of the CDF in response to UI extensions.28
32:1225:79061:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:These estimates suggests that the effect of UI extensions on the CDF of wages for the entire
32:1226:79153:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample is very close to zero. Recall that the effect on the entire CDF is a weighted average of
32:1227:79248:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the effect of the CDF at each nonemployment duration. Hence, since the theory suggests that
32:1228:79339:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reservation wages (and hence the CDF) should rise, the finding of a zero response implies that
32:1229:79433:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the effect of UI extensions on the CDF at each nonemployment duration must be zero. This
32:1230:79521:21:21:68:533:498:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:provides direct evidence that the pattern in Figure 6 (b) are likely to be due to selection.29
32:1231:79615:21:22:85:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The interpretation of our IV estimates as causal effect of nonemployment duration on
32:1232:79699:22:0:68:278:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages relies on our empirical result that
32:1233:79740:0:11:284:317:462:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f16:F:∂wei(t,P)
32:1234:79749:11:17:295:543:451:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:∂Pis approximately zero, which is difficult to
32:1235:79795:17:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:establish empirically with certainty. It is however straightforward to derive bounds for the
32:1236:79887:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of nonemployment durations on wage offers for the case that there are small shifts in the
32:1237:79983:21:0:68:215:392:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:reemployment wage path,∂w
32:1238:80008:0:14:215:238:401:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f16:F:ei(t,P)

33:1318:82847:16:21:68:227:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fourth of the non-stationarity).
33:1319:82879:21:0:85:414:413:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:A:In Table 5, we calculate the impliedπgiven various values ofdV
33:1320:82941:0:13:416:418:422:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:F:ut
33:1321:82943:13:0:410:429:409:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f8:C:dt/
33:1322:82946:0:10:430:442:419:8:g_d0_f10:6:g_d0_f15:F:dVut
33:1323:82950:10:17:432:543:409:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:dPandδ. Essentially
33:1324:82969:17:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as long asδis close to the estimated range in Table 3 (which is always clearly less then 0.1%)
33:1325:83063:22:0:68:92:370:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:ordV
33:1326:83067:0:13:94:95:379:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:F:ut
33:1327:83069:13:0:87:106:366:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f8:C:dt/
33:1328:83072:0:10:107:119:376:8:g_d0_f10:6:g_d0_f15:F:dVut
33:1329:83076:10:17:110:543:366:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:dPis not too high (between -1 and -8) we get values for the change in the slope of the
33:1330:83162:17:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wage offer distribution that are quite close to the IV estimate or even smaller. For example for
33:1331:83258:21:19:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the upper bound of the confidence interval for the pooled estimate in Column (3) of Table 3,
33:1332:83350:19:24:68:544:309:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:ˆδ= 0.095%, the range of slopes for the wage offer distribution is between -1.4% (actually even
33:1333:83445:24:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:smaller than the IV estimate) to -0.7%, just slightly larger than the IV estimate of -0.78%
33:1334:83536:21:38:68:276:264:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:decline in mean wage offers per month.31
33:1335:83576:38:29:68:443:226:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.5  Discussion of Potential Channels Underlying IV Estimates
33:1336:83637:29:22:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As discussed in the theory section, the interpretation of our estimate as the causal effect of
33:1337:83731:22:21:68:543:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment duration is independent of the particular economic model of job search we
33:1338:83818:21:9:68:229:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:which we defer the interested reader.
33:1339:83855:9:7:77:375:145:7:g_d0_f5:5:g_d0_f23:F:31Another source of potential bias in the IV estimator arises ifdht
33:1340:83922:7:9:365:543:138:7:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f6:F:dP= 0, which in our sample occurs for
33:1341:83959:9:13:68:543:129:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:nonemployment durations greater than two years, when benefit durations are exhausted on both sides of the
33:1342:84064:13:0:68:267:116:10:g_d0_f6:7:g_d0_f20:F:age threshold. In that case, even though∂w
33:1343:84106:0:11:267:289:124:5:g_d0_f23:7:g_d0_f22:F:ei(t,P)
33:1344:84113:11:9:267:543:113:7:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f6:F:∂P= 0, fort >24it may be that reservation wages affect
33:1345:84167:9:12:68:543:104:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:accepted wages (i.e., the second term in equation (5) is not zero). Given our results imply no response in
33:1346:84273:12:12:68:543:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:reservation wages fort <24, and given the findings in the literature on the role of reservation wages, we find
33:1347:84383:12:0:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:it safe to assume that the reservation wage effect att >24is likely to be small and this source of bias minor.
34:1348:84495:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used, and holds for a broad range of how wages and outside options are determined. Hence,
34:1349:84584:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:independently of the particular underlying model or source of the effect, the parameter can
34:1350:84675:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be used to gauge the costs of uneployment duration and for assessing the optimal policy mix
34:1351:84766:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in response to nonemployment. However, for some applications it would be helpful to know
34:1352:84854:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more about the channels underlying the effect we find. Several channels have been suggested
34:1353:84945:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the literature.  Using longitudinal data on explicit skill measures from Sweden, Edison
34:1354:85035:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Gustavsson (2008) report that one year of unemployment duration reduces skills by an
34:1355:85123:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equivalent of 0.7 years of schooling, pointing to the potential of skill decline. Kroft, Lange,
34:1356:85218:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Notowidigdo (forthcoming) find that employers discriminate against the long-term un-
34:1357:85306:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:employed, even holding information on education and career progression constant. Similarly,
34:1358:85397:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is some evidence that the unemployed become increasingly unhappy throughout the
34:1359:85482:21:22:68:351:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment spell (e.g., Krueger and Mueller 2011).
34:1360:85535:22:21:85:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our analysis is not geared to uncover the channels underlying the causal effects we find.
34:1361:85624:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Nevertheless, our RD analysis reported in Section 4.3 provides some tentative findings about
34:1362:85716:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:some potential channels.  To assess the potential impact of these effects on reemployment
34:1363:85805:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages, we included these outcomes as additional explanatory variables in our main RD esti-
34:1364:85895:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mates (not shown). Controlling for an indicator capturing industry and occupation changes
34:1365:85984:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:leads to a slight drop in the effect of UI extensions on reemployment wages of 20-25%. Con-
34:1366:86075:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trolling for a part-time indicator and completed tenure at the new job leads to a bit larger
34:1367:86167:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decline of 30-40%. Including proxies for employer quality made no difference. Overall, while
34:1368:86259:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such regressions have to be interpreted with caution, they imply some prima facie evidence of
34:1369:86352:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:role of industry and occupation changes, which have been associated with losses in (industry
34:1370:86444:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or occupation) specific skills in the literature. Similarly, the rise in part-time employment
34:1371:86537:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the reduction in completed job tenure could reflect a decline in job quality. Clearly, some
34:1372:86632:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of these outcomes could reflect several mechanisms, hence we do not stress any particular
34:1373:86721:22:21:68:167:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interpretation here.
34:1374:86741:21:21:85:543:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We have also analyzed differences in the effect of UI extensions on reemployment wages
34:1375:86827:21:21:68:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over the business cycle. On the one hand, if there is statistical discrimination and employ-
34:1376:86919:21:22:68:543:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ers correctly update their priors, the rise in expected mean quality of job applicants during
34:1377:87012:22:21:68:543:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recessions should lead to lower stigma of nonemployment duration. On the other hand, it is
34:1378:87102:21:0:68:543:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plausible that the effect of nonemployment duration on wage offers is stronger in recessions.
35:1379:87197:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For example, there is ample evidence of both a decline in job quality and of a reduction of
35:1380:87288:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages within jobs in recessions, which could hurt in particular workers with longer unemploy-
35:1381:87381:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment spells. When we compare our findings in periods with high and with low unemployment
35:1382:87469:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates, the results are very robust in recessions, but imprecise and ambiguous in expansions
35:1383:87560:21:21:68:495:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(not shown).32Hence, this does not point towards an explanation based on stigma.
35:1384:87640:21:22:85:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, we do not find prima facie evidence in favor of a stigma effect and find some
35:1385:87726:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggestive evidence for skill depreciation. However, our results would also be consistent with
35:1386:87820:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stigma, skill depreciation, and factors such as worker discouragement jointly determining the
35:1387:87913:21:40:68:333:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:causal effect of nonemployment durations on wages.
35:1388:87963:40:33:68:285:501:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6  Summary of Robustness Analysis
35:1389:87996:33:29:68:393:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.1  Robustness of Regression Discontinuity Estimates
35:1390:88049:29:21:68:543:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our main results are all based on a two-year bandwidth around the age thresholds with linear
35:1391:88141:21:21:68:543:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age controls. Focusing on the model pooling both thresholds, Table 6 shows the sensitivity
35:1392:88231:21:22:68:543:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of our results when we allow for more flexibility in the estimation, focusing on five outcome
35:1393:88324:22:21:68:543:375:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables. Columns (2) and (3) show the estimated effects when the bandwidth is reduced
35:1394:88411:21:21:68:543:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to 1 year and 0.5 years. While the sample size drops dramatically and the standard errors
35:1395:88500:21:22:68:543:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase correspondingly, the point estimates all become larger in absolute terms, pointing
35:1396:88591:22:21:68:543:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to worse match outcomes than in the baseline estimates. This pattern is very similar when
35:1397:88680:21:21:68:543:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we control for age with quadratic or cubic polynomials on both sides of the cutoff (columns
35:1398:88771:21:22:68:543:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:3 and 4), where the point estimates are similar to the linear specification with 0.5 years of
35:1399:88864:22:21:68:543:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bandwidth. Using the Calonico et al. (forthcoming) optimal bandwidth algorithm - column
35:1400:88951:21:21:68:543:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(5) - we obtain optimal bandwidths between 0.6 to 0.7 and again slightly more negative wage
35:1401:89042:21:21:68:98:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effecs.
35:1402:89049:21:22:85:543:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In section 3, we reported that we found a slight increase in density just to right of the two
35:1403:89142:22:21:68:543:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age thresholds. Furthermore, we found a small increase in the fraction of female UI recipients
35:1404:89236:21:21:68:543:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at the threshold. Here, we provide several methods to investigate whether this increase will
35:1405:89328:21:19:68:543:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:affect our results. Column (6) of Table 6 shows the results from estimating the marginal effect
35:1406:89423:19:15:77:543:101:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:32The ideal test would hold the distribution of job types constant (comparable to what is done in audit
35:1407:89526:15:12:68:543:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:studies), but is not feasible in our quasi-experimental setting because of small sample sizes and endogeneity
35:1408:89635:12:0:68:110:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:problems.
36:1409:89646:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of potential benefit durations on employment outcomes using our RD design pooling both
36:1410:89732:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thresholds, when we exclude all observations within one month of the age threshold. Overall,
36:1411:89824:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:while excluding the observations close to the cutoff reduces statistical power somewhat, it does
36:1412:89920:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not affect our overall conclusions. Column (7) of Table 6 shows how the estimates change when
36:1413:90013:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we control for a rich set of observables, including year, state, and industry fixed effects, as
36:1414:90108:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well as human capital and experience measures. The effects on nonemployment durations,
36:1415:90194:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the post-unemployment wage, and the duration of the post-unemployment job are slightly
36:1416:90280:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduced but still clearly imply negative match effects. Column (8) of Table 6 shows another
36:1417:90371:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:method robustness check to limit the effect of selective waiting before claiming UI, where we
36:1418:90464:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:limit the sample to individuals who claim UI within two weeks of losing their job.  These
36:1419:90553:21:38:68:307:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects are quite similar to our baseline results.
36:1420:90603:38:29:68:349:460:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.2  Robustness of Estimated Effects on Wages
36:1421:90648:29:21:68:543:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We implemented numerous robustness checks regarding our findings on wages as well. Here,
36:1422:90736:21:22:68:543:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we report results addressing the aspects of selective return to employment, differences in effects
36:1423:90834:22:21:68:524:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across groups, and changes in unemployment rates throughout the nonemployment spell.
36:1424:90918:21:21:85:543:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In Section 4, we have shown that increases in UI extensions lead to precisely estimated
36:1425:91005:21:22:68:543:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:declines in the incidence of employment (Table 1). While these effects were very small relative
36:1426:91100:22:21:68:543:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the mean (less than 1%), we investigated the potential effect of such selection on our
36:1427:91189:21:21:68:543:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates of the effect of UI durations on wages by analyzing differences in the quantiles of
36:1428:91282:21:21:68:543:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the distribution of outcomes on the two sides of the age cutoffs (shown in the Web Appendix).
36:1429:91375:21:22:68:543:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This standard procedure yields consistent estimates if selection depends monotonously on a
36:1430:91465:22:21:68:543:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:single index of underlying characteristics.  The results suggest that the decline in median
36:1431:91556:21:21:68:543:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages is larger than the mean effect, suggesting that if at all our main findings underestimate
36:1432:91651:21:22:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the effect of UI extensions on wages. Moreover, the lower percentiles of the wage distribution
36:1433:91745:22:21:68:543:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decline more strongly than the upper percentiles, , implying that the majority of wage declines
36:1434:91840:21:21:68:439:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in response to UI extensions occurr in the lower part of the distribution.
36:1435:91914:21:22:85:543:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The concern of selective participation also arises when studying reemployment wages at
36:1436:92000:22:21:68:543:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each point in the nonemployment spell.  As long as selection into employment for the full
36:1437:92089:21:21:68:543:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample is not an issue, our procedure for controlling for dynamic selection in Table 3 also
36:1438:92180:21:0:68:543:69:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:controls for the effects of selective participation when estimating the effect of UI extensions
37:1439:92277:0:21:68:296:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the shift in the reemployment wage path.
37:1440:92320:21:21:85:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In Section 5, we had said that part of the effect on reemployment wages at the exhaustion
37:1441:92409:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points month 12 and month 18 are likely to be due to a change in sample composition. In par-
37:1442:92501:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ticular, there is a rise in the fraction of women to the right of the RD cutoffs, and a rise in the
37:1443:92600:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fraction of women exiting at the exhaustion points. To address this point, we have replicated
37:1444:92693:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our main RD analysis and our analysis of reemployment wages by gender. Women’s nonem-
37:1445:92778:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ployment durations clearly respond more strongly to UI extensions (Schmieder, von Wachter,
37:1446:92868:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Bender 2012a), there is no precisely estimated difference in the effect on reemployment
37:1447:92959:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages by gender. As a result, the implied IV estimate of the effect of nonemployment dura-
37:1448:93049:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions on wages is somewhat smaller for women, and approximately the same for men. Hence,
37:1449:93137:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our main findings are robust for the small degree of selection of women into nonemployment
37:1450:93227:21:22:68:207:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and UI exhaustion we find.
37:1451:93253:22:21:85:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another potential concern is that our main analysis focuses on workers with comparatively
37:1452:93342:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high labor force attachment for whom nonemployment spells might be particularly costly. As
37:1453:93432:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed in Section 3, we can replicate our IV strategy for any worker eligible for UI. For this
37:1454:93529:21:22:68:544:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:broader sample, Table 4 shows we obtain a somewhat larger estimate of−1.2%for the age 42
37:1455:93617:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cutoff, and−1.5%when we pool both cutoffs, where only the latter is statistically significant
37:1456:93710:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from our main sample.33Thus, our findings are not driven by the particular sample we use,
37:1457:93799:21:22:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and hold for a broad sample of middle aged workers in Germany. We also considered the effect
37:1458:93891:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of UI durations and nonemployment durations on wages for other subgroups, but statistical
37:1459:93980:21:39:68:364:285:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:precision was low and hence did not pursue this further.34
37:1460:94038:39:33:68:152:246:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:7  Conclusion
37:1461:94051:33:22:68:543:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The effect of unemployment durations on job outcomes has important implications for policy
37:1462:94141:22:21:68:543:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at the micro and macro level. Using an IV strategy based on quasi-experimental extensions
37:1463:94230:21:21:68:543:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in UI benefits we find that for middle aged workers each additional month of nonemployment
37:1464:94320:21:18:68:543:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duration leads to a statistically significant and substantial reduction in wage offers of 0.8%. We
37:1465:94418:18:15:77:543:131:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:33The difference in the size of the IV estimate is mainly driven by a smaller effect of UI extensions on
37:1466:94522:15:12:68:543:116:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:nonemployment durations, which is to be expected since the average rise of potential UI durations is smaller
37:1467:94630:12:9:68:407:104:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:for this group. The corresponding estimates are shown in the Web Appendix.
37:1468:94704:9:15:77:543:95:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:34For example, while lower educated workers had substantially larger responses in employment duration,
37:1469:94806:15:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the effect of UI durations on wage changes appeared only slightly larger for the lower educated, implying a
37:1470:94913:12:0:68:458:68:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:smaller (but not precisely estimated) causal effect of nonemployment durations on wages.
38:1471:95003:0:21:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show that this estimate identifies a weighted average of the slope of the wage offer distribution
38:1472:95100:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for individuals whose nonemployment durations are affected by the UI extensions. Given that
38:1473:95191:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UI durations lead to a decline in reemployment probabilities throughout the nonemployment
38:1474:95280:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spell, it is relevant for a broad group of unemployed workers. In our setting, over six to twelve
38:1475:95377:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:months this can explain about a third of wage losses from unemployment. These estimates
38:1476:95464:21:22:68:478:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are smaller than existing estimates with non-experimental controls for selection.
38:1477:95545:22:21:85:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our IV strategy is based on the key insight that the response of reemployment wages to UI
38:1478:95634:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:extensions throughout the nonemployment spell is informative about the role of reservation
38:1479:95724:21:22:68:543:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages even if the degree of selection is arbitrarily affected by UI durations. Our finding that
38:1480:95819:22:21:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the path of reemployment wages over nonemployment duration does not shift in response to
38:1481:95907:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UI extensions implies that reservation wages do not bind. Hence, the UI extensions only affect
38:1482:96001:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wages through a rise in unemployment durations and hence can be used as an instrument for
38:1483:96090:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-employment durations.  We also analyzed the response of different points in the wage
38:1484:96178:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution to UI extensions. While we do observe some small shifts in the lower quantiles
38:1485:96269:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates in response to UI extensions, these changes appear to be due to selection.  In a
38:1486:96359:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bounding exercise, we show that our main results are robust to small and realistic effects of
38:1487:96452:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reservation wages. The framework we develop here for the analysis of the causal effects of
38:1488:96542:21:21:68:543:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment durations on wages and other job outcomes will be useful for other studies
38:1489:96630:21:22:68:541:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that analyze the effects of exogenous changes in wokers outside options on worker outcomes.
38:1490:96721:22:21:85:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our findings can be used to help quantify the earnings losses from long unemployment spells
38:1491:96812:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for workers. They also affect the optimal policy mix in response to long-term unemployment
38:1492:96902:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and suggest that both at the micro- and macro-level policies should be front loaded to avoid
38:1493:96994:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the substatial cost associated with long-term unemployment. The results are also potentially
38:1494:97086:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:informative about the effects of prolonged nonemployment spells on the aggregate economy.
38:1495:97175:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our findings suggest that these can lead to persistent and substantial declines in wages that
38:1496:97268:22:21:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appear to be larger in recessions. In so far as workers may be receiving lower job matches or
38:1497:97361:21:21:68:543:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have lower productivity, this could imply a significant cost to society going beyond the direct
38:1498:97456:21:21:68:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cost of unemployment itself. However, by construction our regression discontinuity analysis
38:1499:97547:21:22:68:543:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is partial equilibrium in nature, and a full evaluation of the implications of causal effects of
38:1500:97643:22:21:68:543:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment we document here would require specifying the source of the losses and a
38:1501:97729:21:0:68:184:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:macroeconomic model.
39:1502:97751:0:21:85:543:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:While we find unemployment duration has potentially large effects on wages, the small
39:1503:97836:21:21:68:543:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:underlying effect of UI extensions on wages may not substantially affect the welfare conse-
39:1504:97927:21:22:68:543:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quences of UI extensions. If individuals get all the surplus from higher match quality, then
39:1505:98019:22:21:68:543:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they will have internalized the effect of their search behavior on match quality, and the effects
39:1506:98116:21:21:68:543:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of potential UI durations on match quality can be ignored from a social welfare perspective.
39:1507:98208:21:22:68:543:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This situation is different, if workers do not reap all the benefits of better matches—for ex-
39:1508:98302:22:21:68:543:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ample, because the surplus is shared with the employer or because the government receives
39:1509:98391:21:21:68:543:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:taxes. Even in the latter case, the small direct effects of UI extensions on wages we find are
39:1510:98485:21:22:68:386:541:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:unlikely to imply a substantial rise in costs of UI extensions.35
39:1511:98550:22:21:85:543:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our results are also related to the value of leisure. Rational individuals incur the costs
39:1512:98640:21:21:68:543:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of additional wage reductions above and beyond foregone earnings during nonemployment
39:1513:98725:21:22:68:543:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in favor of additional leisure. A back-of-the-envelope calculation suggests that the present
39:1514:98817:22:21:68:543:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discounted value of the cost from lower wages due to higher nonemployment durations is
39:1515:98903:21:21:68:543:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about half a month of average earnings per additional month of nonemployment duration.
39:1516:98989:21:21:68:543:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This may indeed be rational, in so far fixed costs of working or fixed costs of leaving a job
39:1517:99082:21:22:68:543:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:put a wedge between the value of leisure and foregone earnings. Yet, it also could be that
39:1518:99172:22:21:68:543:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individuals do not fully foresee the wage penalty they incur. Without additional information
39:1519:99264:21:21:68:392:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and estimating structural parameters we cannot say more here.
39:1520:99325:21:22:85:543:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Last but not least, by the nature of our regression discontinuity design and institutional
39:1521:99415:22:21:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:framework, our estimates are based on middle age workers with stable labor force attach-
39:1522:99503:21:21:68:543:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment. While this is the core constituency of unemployment insurance in Germany, the United
39:1523:99593:21:22:68:543:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:States and other countries, it does not speak to the potential effects of UI durations and
39:1524:99683:22:21:68:543:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonemployment durations for a broader population. Studies with data and research designs
39:1525:99771:21:21:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:encompassing broader groups of workers will help to obtain additional information on how the
39:1526:99863:21:22:68:543:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects we measure here differ in the population, what the likely effect on the macroeconomy is,
39:1527:99959:22:21:68:543:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and what the underlying channels may be. Similarly, while we showed in our precursor paper
39:1528:100049:21:21:68:543:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the characteristics of our sample is comparable to similarly aged UI recipients in the
39:1529:100140:21:21:68:543:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:United States and that the effect of UI durations on employment are comparable (Schmieder,
39:1530:100230:21:19:68:543:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:von Wachter, and Bender 2012a), one has to be careful in generalizing from our results based
39:1531:100322:19:16:77:543:96:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:35This is essentially an application of the envelope theorem. See Chetty (2008) and Schmieder, von Wachter,
39:1532:100429:16:11:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and Bender (2012a) for details. Nekoei and Weber (2013) show that foregone tax revenues from lower earnings
39:1533:100536:11:0:68:155:69:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:can also play a role.
40:1534:100559:0:53:68:133:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on Germany.
40:1535:100570:53:27:68:131:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:References
